Don't play Genshin, follow it for the music. To me, this song feels like the good guys, overconfident or mischievious, eventually lost their battle in the end. The short burst at the last ten seconds or so makes it feel like it was their last push. There is always a theme to this game's music, it always hits you with a loud, confident, or dramatic section than shifts into a solemn, melancholy feel.  The mix of orchestra, opera, electric instruments, acoustic guitar, edm and so on always catches me off guard! (ignoring character voices.) 0:55 This brass gives a hidden sadness vibe 2:55 The organ which symbolizes holiness makes me feel like there is something immensely dangerous in either one big destructive entity or some overseeing oppressive force. 3:35 The intense percussion and the choir shows that there is some looming entity suppressing this region. Also sounds like an intense movie trailer. 4:05 Soloist opera singer reminds me of La Signora's battle theme, but instead of tragic, it sounds dramatic for the trailer. 4:20 Love the series of pauses, it adds suspense but also acts as a reset. A palate cleanser if you will. 4:28 Like that off sounding key. Minor? Flat? Idk. 4:32 Where did this electric guitar come from? It sounds like one last push to victory. Very unsatisfactory or unusual ending to the ear. Leaves the listener feeling down, anxious, or uncomfortable. But it ends with a lower note compared to the higher music before it, which to me signifies resolve. So it sounds like the good guys loosing.  Genshin's music composers and producers are back again to produce top notch and striking pieces of art!

time to claim another god
Okay I have a theory. Just humor me here, take it with a grain of salt (but please don't be rude). For me, characters with hydro visions are those that exhibit DUALITY and adaptability to go with the flow (like Childe, Ayato, Yelan and Kokomi), hence the versatility it provides in most team comps. Needless to say, hydro is one of the strongest elements. On the other hand, the hydro abyss mages show us one extreme case of how hydro can literally imprison characters. And, if not applied with the correct strategy, it is very difficult to deal with hydro bosses. You could be level 90 but good luck trying to kill Rhodeia with a full hydro non-physical team. Those hydro mimics deal insane damage. You might not stagger fighting them but before you know it, you're already at 1hp. Heck, Rhodeia even heals them if you don't kill them fast enough. All this tells how hydro as an element has two sides to it: the healing one and the extremely painful one. Similar to Anemo, Hydro "goes with the flow" but unlike Anemo that literally says "idgaf", Hydro is grounded in reality. Hydro possessors literally "go with the flow" whether it's the good or the bad side to fulfill a goal that they are deadset on. Now what does that remind us of? POLITICS. Exactly. The concept that has been publicized about Fontaine and its archon so far is that their courtroom is a "theatre" of sorts. This is like that age old adage: "POLITICS IS A FARCE" Here, there is no real "justice" and there is no real right or wrong. The thing is, "justice" is apparently the wish and desire of the people of Fontaine. And we all know that Archons are only given power based on their respective people's faith. It will not be far off to see that the current hydro archon has been driven mad (as in mentally unstable) with the "justice" that her people desperately wish for because their "justice" mean different things depending on which faction you ask, but in general, it results in the fall of their enemies--and if their enemies are fellow believers, well obviously it gets confusing. It's like there's always 2 sides to a coin but if it's like that, then how can you judge who is right and who is wrong? A huge indicator of this duality factor is the different eyes and face decals the hydro archon has on either side: one is weeping while the other has a star. Basically saying yes, the hydro archon has been driven mad by the demands of her people for their own respective "justices". She can just annihilate whoever she doesn't like but in the name of "justice", she cannot. Her power over "justice" ironically has made her prisoner. The thing is, while water flows gently in a peaceful spring, it is relentless in the torrential rapids and an absolute hell in the storm. Rain never discriminates. "Light rain falls without reason." If pushed to the edge, she can just deliver her own "justice" to the hypocrites who have been using her (the divide among citizens no doubt instigated by the Fatui). The hydro archon probably knows how dangerously close she is to exploding and drowning everyone in her madness so her last remaining sanity is seeking for help. Or the more likely one is that, going further along the DUALITY concept, being the hydro archon of a land where there's literally water everywhere, she probably already knows what is going on behind the scenes and is acting The Fool (won't be hard, she's already crazy), going along with the flow to keep her citizens from becoming hostages until comes a time where she can find a decent helper to put her plans in motion and wreak havoc without harming her people. And I guess that's where the traveller enters the scene and sorts out all the wrinkles.

I'm still playing, but I'm already pretty tired of the scam system in the game: scam in twists (3 guarantors flew away to the Song of Broken Pines) and even more fierce scam in artifacts. It is necessary to introduce a guarantor for artifacts: for example, for 199 a player receives random artifacts, and for 200 - a guaranteed artifact he needs with crits. Why only 200? Yes, because there is no guarantee that at the point of the artifact the rolls will fly into the cherished crit damage / crit chance. If you give everything at once to the player, this is bad - but on the other hand, if the player does not get what he deserves for months, he starts to leave, and the solvent audience leaves, buying at least the Moon and BP. So the Chinese should think about this as soon as possible, otherwise, with their scams, they themselves will cut down the branch on which they sit, that is, their breadwinners.

Iâ€™M SO EXCITED!! â¤
Judging by the trailer and the special program, it seems that the Oratrice, which generates the energy of Fontaine runs on the belief people in Fontaine have of justice. (And thus court trials are treated like theatre for entertainment and it likely explains why laws are so strict; so they can use any excuse to begin a trial to generate more energy and provide entertainment) However as Lynette mentioned the Oratrice is swallowing memories and even entire people by some mysterious method, it seems that Lyney and Lynette were sent undercover to discover the secrets of how it operates to stop "The Prophecy" which was mentioned at the beginning, that is that the people of Fontaine will be dissolved into water leading to the Hydro archon being alone to mourn. This seems like the main plot of Fontaine as we see Lynette disappear during her and Lyneys show, at 3:40 with Paimon(?) asking "Is this part of the show?"   It seems that they were performing in the court which also functions as the opera room, it is likley that the Oratrices powers did something to Lynette since its location would have been at the centre of the court, it is likely that it caused her to disappear.   We'll likely see this as the first event of the archon quest, arriving in Fontaine only to see a performer disappear in the middle of a show, sending us on a wild mystery hunt as to how the Oratrice is doing this, where we team up with Navia to put a stop to the corrupt justice system.   Honestly theres so much more to say but after my initial excitement dying down these are my major takeaways from the trailer, it looks fantastic and I am very stoked.   (Also I just wanted to mention that 4:05 - 4:24 has such fantastic cinematography and the dialogue really nails home the overarching problem that Furina just doesn't care about delivering true justice but would rather put people on trial to watch their lives be molded as if their livelihoods are meant for her entertainment.)  Honestly though this plot could go any way, but the plot is very intriguing to me and I'm totally ready to see more.

**Spoilers for Fontaine Trailer**  My own theory for Fontaine is that there is a beast in the water draining memories or part of the mechanism of Fontaine. They mentioned energy blocks keep Fontaine running but never said how those were obtained. We see the courthouse and a unique mechanism where the criminals disappear, I theorize that that's how they harvest memories. The courthouse might also have vision blocking properties as we see Childe without his vision. That might be because that mechanism is limited to the courthouse. We also see the Electro captain use her vision with the machines, making it fair to assume that there is a mechanism and its limited to the courthouse so that people can't cause trouble. In that space, only the hydro archon has any power. WIth the exception of the traveler and delusion users as we see with childe. The dialogue from Oceanid further supports that a darker power lurks with "corrupted waters" and itself seeks for tranquil waters. So its likely a mechanism or a beast that lies beneath the surface of Fontaine.

In the most recent desert map's world quest, we discover that a Fontaine expidition team found an energy source called Azosite, along with some other findings, that they would bring back with them. I bet that what they discovered back then is what is powering Fontaine currently. In the livestream they mention a woman invented energy blocks with the Arkhe reaction over 400 years ago(so just after the Cataclysm), but as we learn in Sumeru, Ruin Guard machines are also powered by a thing called Energy Blocks, which means yep, Fontaine is being powered by Khaenri'an tech. The same Khaenri'ah that was destroyed for their tech not following the Heavenly Principles' guidelines. And I bet Fontaine doesnt have a very good understanding of the tech either, which means it's much more likely that something will go wrong. Either bad things are happening because they don't know how to take care of it properly, or it's the Heavenly Principles punishing them for using illegal technology

My proposed analysis of the trailer:   0:00 - 0:18 The foretold prophecy reminds me of the Third Impact from Evangelion. Where everyone became part of the human instrumentality project. I theorize that this prophecy would have every inhabitant of Fontaine turn into water the same way as in Evangelion.   2:47 The depicted scene prior to diving underwater shows a shattered city, probably Fontaine when the prophecy happens. If this scene is true, this means that Celestia (who is currently above Fontaine; per theorists), has dropped another spear (like over Dragonspine) onto Fontaine.  This makes it the second possibility / outcome of the aforementioned prophecy.   2:52  The character we see is probably an Oceanid. Some seconds later, we see Aether in the void with her. Judging from past experience, we can safely suppose that Aether has entered the Oceanid's consciousness [world]; just like with Nahida during the Sumeru Archon Quest.   3:15 Lyney mentions that the Oratrice has a consciousness of its own. Saying that it delivers a very accurate judgement at each sentencing. My theory is that Fontaine's court depends on the Oratrice for delivering each and every sentence since it started operation.  Tying this system to my previous statement, I would like to theorize that inhabiting the machine is an imprisoned Oceanid. One who's been in there for so long that she no longer remembers anything. But can only deliver a judgement at the bequest of either Focalors (Furina) or Neuvillette.  I suppose that it is up to Aether to liberate whoever was imprisoned in the Oratrice.  By the way, Oratrice is French for female speaker.   3:44 Lynette just disappears from the water tank at the same time as time stopped. It must be said that seconds ago, it started raining.   We know that Navia was surprised if not terrified when it started to rain. Note that when Fontaine was presented in all trailers (up to date), not once has it rained. Whereas in other regions, when it rained, it was a natural occurence, not a surprising one.  I don't have much to say about that, but it is open to speculation.   3:59 At this time, we can see Navia and her "Men in Black" (MIB). All of them seem to be helping / protecting the traveller from the Gardemeks (robots) and Chlorinde. What we can theorize is that they (Navia + MIB) are part of an underground organisation that are secretly acting against the current Fontaine administration.   4:03 Chlorinde uses the Iron Sting as her main weapon. Finally a 5-star (?) character that has it as a canon weapon.   4:20 Why is Childe there? What is his purpose? I can only theorize 2 things (up to interpretation):  - 1) Aether probably sent Childe a "HELP" letter and he directly came to help due to it aligning with his (Childe's) agenda.  - 2) Childe is in Fontaine because Arlecchino (The Knave) has went rogue (like Scaramouche) and he was tasked with a capture or kill mission. But so happened to get caught up in the Traveller's shenanigans (i.e. his trial).   Random side notes:   - The final trial was aimed directly at Aether judging by the timing of Lynette's disappearance and the battle with the Gardemeks.  - The trial part would mark the half-way point in the Archon Quest, where he'd go underground with Navia and the MIBs to organize a counter-attack.  - Childe seems to appear quite late in the Archon Quest. Possibly during the final missions to fight the Gardemeks and directly confront both Focalors (Furina) and Neuvillette.  - We can expect Navia and Chlorinde to be fighting each other regularly (please do not start shipping them for just this reason). So Aether would equally be involved in the fightings.  - Arlecchino has not appeared once in this trailer. Which is extremely worrying as it signifies an appearance at an unknown moment (like with Dottore).  - Btw, we haven't seen the following characters: Charlotte, Wriothesley and Siegwinne.  - In the trailer, there were some fantasy-like underground locations (villages), which could be the homes of the MÃ©lusine people.   That will be all for now.
